[Atharvan,тАФekonanavati.1 yamadevatyam mantroktabahtidevatyaс╣Б ca (81. pitс╣Ыdevatyam;2 88. ─Бgney─л; 89. c─Бndramas─л). tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham: 1, 4, 7, 14, 36, 60. bhurij; 2, 5, 11, 29, 50, 51, 58. jagat─л; 3. 5-p. bhurig atijagat─л; 6, 9, 13. 5-p. ┼Ыakvar─л (9. bhurij; 13. 3-av.); 8. 5-p. ati┼Ыakvar─л; 12. mah─Бbс╣Ыhat─л; 16-24. 3-p. bhurin╠Д mah─Бbс╣Ыhat─л; 26, 33, [43]. upariс╣гс╣н─Бdbс╣Ыhat─л3 (26. vir─Бj); 27. y─Бjuс╣г─л g─Бyatr─л; [25], 31, 32, 38, 41, 42, 55-57, 59, 61. anuс╣гс╣нubh3 (56. kakummat─л); 39, 62, 63. ─Бst─Бrapan╠Дkti (39. purovir─Бj; 62. bhurij; 63. svar─Бj); 49. anuс╣гс╣нubgarbh─Б triс╣гс╣нubh; 53. purovir─Бс╣н sataс╕еpan╠Дkti; 66. 3-p. svar─Бс╕Н g─Бyatr─л; 67. 2-p. ─Бrcy anuс╣гс╣нubh; 68, 71. ─Бsury anuс╣гс╣нubh; 72-74, 79. ─Бsur─л pan╠Дkti; 75. ─Бsur─л g─Бyatr─л; 76. ─Бsury uс╣гс╣Зih; 77. d─Бiv─л jagat─л; 78. ─Бsuri triс╣гс╣нubh; 80. ─Бsur─л jagat─л; 81. pr─Бj─Бpaty─Б тАЩnuс╣гс╣нubh; 82. s─Бmn─л bс╣Ыhat─л; 83, 84. s─Бmn─л triс╣гс╣нubh; 83. ─Бsur─л bс╣Ыhat─л (67-68, 71-86. 1-av.)4; 86, 87. 4-p. uс╣гс╣Зih (86. kakummat─л; 87. ┼Ыan╠Дkumat─л); 88. 3-av. pathy─Бpan╠Дkti; 89. 3-p. pathy─Бpan╠Дkti.]

Comment

The translation implies emendation in a to j─Бtavedasas, though all the mss., and hence both editions, read j─Бt├бv-; all, also, accent in c havyav─Б╠Бhas, and SPP. has that in his text; our edition makes the obviously necessary emendation to -v─Бh├бs тМКcf. the opposite error in vs. 10тМЛ. All our saс╣Бhita-mss. тМКsee Pr─Бt. i. 94, noteтМЛ make in c the false combination ├бv─Бс╕Нh с╕Нh-; SPP. says nothing of his, and both editions have correctly ├бv─Бс╕Н с╕Нh-. Our O.Op.R., and one of SPP’s mss., read in c iс╣гit─Б╠Б; the comm. also has it, explaining it with iс╣гit─Бny iс╣гс╣н─Бni. The comm. also understands j─Бtavedasas as vocative (probably, after his manner, simply disregarding the accent); he explains janitr─лm as svotp─Бdik─Бm araс╣Зim; and the K─Бu┼Ы. (80. 23) takes the same view: iti pс╣Ыtha┼Ы araс╣З─лс╣гv agn─лn sam─Бropayanti; but its correctness as original sense of the verse may be strongly questioned. The comm. explains ─Б rohata by ┼Ыakty─Бtman─Б pravi┼Ыata; and describes the sam─Бropaс╣Зa as taking place “because of the absence of any further ceremonies to be performed by him, being now dead, by help of the fires.” In the comm’s viniyoga he says simply araс╣Зidvayam agn─Бu prat─Бpayet. All this is in the case of a person who has died away from home. But vss. 1-15 are also used nearly at the end of the cremation ceremony (K─Бu┼Ы. 81. 45), with the direction ity ─Бhit─Бgnim (Ke┼Ы. adds upatiс╣гс╣нhate), тМКand the comm. fills out the direction thus: citistham ─Бhit─Бgnim pretam upatiс╣гс╣нhetaтМЛ. The verse, as a triс╣гс╣нubh, is redundant by a syllable тМКin a, which is thus a good jagat─л-p─Бda: and also by one in d, which, however, by reason of its triс╣гс╣нubh cadence, is neither one thing nor the otherтМЛ.

Griffith

A funeral hymn, composed partly of verses from the Rigveda

Whitney
Translation
  1. Ascend to [your] generatrix, ye J─Бtavedases; by [roads] that the
    Fathers travel I make you ascend together; the offering-carrier, sent
    out, hath carried the offerings; united (yukt├б), set ye him who hath
    sacrificed in the world of the well-doing.

Griffith

Rise to your mother, flames of Jatavedas! I send you up by paths which Fathers traverse. With headlong speed the Oblation bearer bore our gifts: toil ye, and place the offerer where the righteous dwell.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЬрд╛рддрд╡реЗрджрд╕рдГ) рдмрдбрд╝реЗрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рддреБрдо (рдЬрдирд┐рддреНрд░реАрдореН) рдЬрдЧрддреН рдХреА рдЬрдирдиреА [рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛] рдХреЛ (рдЖ) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдк рдХрд░ (рд░реЛрд╣рдд)рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯ рд╣реЛрдУ, (рдкрд┐рддреГрдпрд╛рдгреИрдГ) рдкрд┐рддрд░реЛрдВ [рдкрд╛рд▓рдХ рдорд╣рд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдУрдВ] рдХреЗ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рд╕рдореН) рдорд┐рд▓рдХрд░ (рд╡рдГ)рддреБрдореНрд╣реЗрдВ (рдЖ рд░реЛрд╣рдпрд╛рдорд┐) рдореИрдВ [рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН] рдКрдБрдЪрд╛ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реВрдБред (рдЗрд╖рд┐рддрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд┐рдп (рд╣рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╛рд╣рдГ)рджреЗрдиреЗ-рд▓реЗрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдкрд╣реБрдБрдЪрд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдиреЗ (рд╣рд╡реНрдпрд╛) рджреЗрдиреЗ-рд▓реЗрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде (рдЕрд╡рд╛рдЯреН) рдкрд╣реБрдБрдЪрд╛рдП рд╣реИрдВ, (рдИрдЬрд╛рдирдореН) рдпрдЬреНрдЮ рдХрд░ рдЪреБрдХрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рдХреЛ (рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ)рдорд┐рд▓реЗ рд╣реБрдП рддреБрдо (рд╕реБрдХреГрддрд╛рдореН) рд╕реБрдХрд░реНрдорд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рд▓реЛрдХреЗ) рд╕рдорд╛рдЬ рдореЗрдВ (рдзрддреНрдд) рд░рдХреНрдЦреЛ реерезрее

Whitney
Translation
  1. The gods, the seasons, arrange the sacrifice, the oblation, the
    sacrificial cake, the ladles (sr├║c), the implements (-─Б╠Бyudha) of
    sacrifice; with them go thou by roads that the gods travel, by which
    they that have sacrificed go to the heavenly (svarg├б) world.
Notes

The word sruc├бs in b is shown by the meter to be probably an
intrusion, and it is superfluous as regards the sense. тМКThe excision of
hav├нs would give a better cesura.тМЛ The verse is, of course, in no way
a real jagat─л. K─Бu┼Ы. (81. 10) directs it to be used as a sacrificial
cake is laid on the breast of the corpse on the funeral pile; the comm.
takes no notice of this.

Griffith

The Seasons, Deities, form and order Worship, butter, cake, ladles, sacrificial weapons. Tread thou God-travelled paths whereby the righteous, payers of sacrifices, go to Svarga.

рдкрджрдкрд╛рдардГ

рджреЗреТрд╡рд╛рдГред рдпреТрдЬреНрдЮрдореНред рдЛреТрддрд╡рдГреСред рдХреТрд▓реНрдкреТрдпреТрдиреНрддрд┐реТред рд╣реТрд╡рд┐рдГред рдкреБреТрд░реЛреТрдбрд╛рд╢реСрдореНред рд╕реНрд░реБреТрдЪрдГред рдпреТрдЬреНрдЮреТрд╜рдЖреТрдпреБреТрдзрд╛рдирд┐реСред рддреЗрднрд┐рдГреСред рдпрд╛реТрд╣рд┐реТред рдкреТрдерд┐рд╜рднрд┐рдГреСред рджреЗреТрд╡реТрд╜рдпрд╛рдиреИрдГреСред рдпреИрдГред рдИреТрдЬрд╛реТрдирд╛рдГред рд╕реНрд╡рдГреТрд╜рдЧрдореНред рдпрдиреНрддрд┐реСред рд▓реЛреТрдХрдореНред рек.реиред

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рд╕рддреНрдп рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рдкрд░ рдЪрд▓рдиреЗ рдХрд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд▓реЛрдЧрдФрд░ (рдЛрддрд╡рдГ) рд╕рдм рдЛрддреБрдПрдБ (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН) рдпрдЬреНрдЮ [рд╣рд╡рди рдЖрджрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░], (рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ) рд╣рд╡рд┐ [рд╣реЛрдореАрдп рд╡рд╕реНрддреБ], (рдкреБрд░реЛрдбрд╛рд╢рдореН) рдкреБрд░реЛрдбрд╛рд╢ [рдореЛрд╣рдирднреЛрдЧ рдЖрджрд┐], (рд╕реНрд░реБрдЪрдГ) рд╕реНрд░реБрдЪрд╛рдУрдВ [рд╣рд╡рди рдХреЗрдЪрдордЪреЛрдВ] рдФрд░ (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпреБрдзрд╛рдирд┐) рдпрдЬреНрдЮ рдХреЗ рдЕрд╕реНрддреНрд░-рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЛрдВ [рдЙрд▓реВрдЦрд▓, рдореВрд╕рд▓, рд╕реВрдк рдЖрджрд┐] рдХреЛ (рдХрд▓реНрдкрдпрдиреНрддрд┐) рд░рдЪрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВред [рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп !] (рддреЗрднрд┐рдГ) рдЙрди (рджреЗрд╡рдпрд╛рдиреИрдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЪрд▓рдиреЗрдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рдкрдерд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рдпрд╛рд╣рд┐) рддреВ рдЪрд▓, (рдпреИрдГ) рдЬрд┐рди [рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЛрдВ] рд╕реЗ (рдИрдЬрд╛рдирд╛рдГ) рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдХрд░ рдЪреБрдХрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд▓реЛрдЧ (рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЧрдореН) рд╕реБрдЦ рдкрд╣реБрдБрдЪрд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рд▓реЛрдХрдореН) рд╕рдорд╛рдЬ рдореЗрдВ (рдпрдиреНрддрд┐) рдкрд╣реБрдБрдЪрддреЗрд╣реИрдВ реереирее

Translation
  1. Look thou happily (s─Бdh├║) along the road of righteousness, by which
    go the An╠Дgirases, well-doers; by those roads go thou to heaven
    (svarg├б), where the ─Аdityas feed on honey; spread thou out upon the
    third firmament.
Notes

two of SPP’s mss., read t├йbhyas at beginning of c. The comm.
explains v├н┼Ыrayasva in e by vi┼Ыritaс╕е pratiс╣гс╣нhito bhava. The
metrical description of the Anukr. fits the verse, if we тМКdecline to
make two of the three easy resolutions (in c and d) by which the
verse reads as five good triс╣гс╣нubh p─БdasтМЛ.

Griffith

Carefully look on Sacrifice’s pathway whereon the Angirases, the righteous, travel. By those same pathways go thou up to Svarga where the Adityas take their fill of sweetness, There make thy home in the third vault of heaven,

Whitney
Translation
  1. Three eagles (suparс╣З├б)…upon the back of the firmament (n─Б╠Бka),
    at the summit (? viс╣гс╣н├бp) are set (┼Ыrit├б); let the heavenly
    (svarg├б) worlds, filled (?) with amс╣Ы╠Бta, yield (duh) food,
    refreshment to the sacrificer.
Notes

The pada-text reads in a m─Бy┼л╠Б ├нti, which is, I presume, intended
to mark the word as a locative: see Pr─Бt. i. 74 and note upon it. The
comm., however, understands it as dual, and explains it as meaning
m─Бyumant─Бu ┼Ыabdak─Бriс╣З─Бu v─Бyuparjany─Бu, because V─Бyu and Parjanya are
noisy in connection with clouds; for upara, by Nirukta 2. 21, means ‘a
cloud’; and the three eagles are Agni, S┼лrya, and Soma! the general
sense being that V─Бyu and Parjanya are set over the world of the
atmosphere, and the other three over the heavenly world! In c, the
translation follows the comm. тМКand Whitney’s P.M.I, and one of SPP’s
mss.тМЛ in reading viс╣гс╣н─Б╠Бs instead of viс╣гс╣нh─Б╠Бs (p. viре░sth─Б╠Бс╕е); it is
glossed with vy─Бpt─Бс╕е p┼лrс╣З─Бс╕е. Neither this verse nor the preceding is
quoted by K─Бu┼Ы., nor has either a viniyoga indicated in the comm.

Griffith

Three eagles in the region’s roar are standing high on heaven’s ridge in their appointed station. The worlds of Svarga shall, filled full of Amrit, yield food and power to him who sacrificeth.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The sacrificial spoon (juh┼л╠Б) sustains the sky, the offering spoon
    (upabhс╣Ы╠Бt) the atmosphere; the ladle (dhruv─Б╠Б) sustains тМКdhс╣ЫтМЛ the
    earth, the support (pratiс╣гс╣нh─Б╠Б); unto me (?) let the worlds,
    ghee-backed, heavenly (svarg├б), yield every desire for the sacrificer.
Notes

The reading and sense at the beginning of c are very doubtful; the
pada-mss. all give pratiре░m─Б╠Бm, as if it were accusative of pratim─Б╠Б;
most of the saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. have prat─лm─Б╠Бm (our Bs. has prat├нm─Б╠Бm тМК!тМЛ,
and P.M. pratim─Б╠Бm; T. has prat─лm├бm), and it is quoted in the comment
to the Pr─Бt. (ii. 35: so the ms.) as the same тМКthat is, I presume, in
the form prat─лm─БmтМЛ. SPP. emends to pr├бt─л тАЩm─Б╠Бm, since, with his usual
disregard of the accent, the comm. so reads, explaining im─Бm as
referring to pс╣Ыthiv─лm; our edition has pratim─Б╠Бm, with the majority
of our earlier mss. The translation implies pr├бti m─Б╠Бm, simply on
account of superior intelligibility; doubtless the true AV. reading is
prat─лm─Б╠Бm. Simply pr├бti would rectify the meter, and give a yet
better sense. The verse (13 + 11: 12 (11?) + 11 = 47) is, of course, no
proper jagat─л. This and the verse next following are used, according
to K─Бu┼Ы. 81. 7, as the sacrificial utensils are laid about and upon the
body, to be burned with it.

Griffith

Upabhrit stablished air, Juhu the heaven, Dhruva supported earth securely founded. As meed, the Svarga worlds, o’erspread with fatness shall yield the sacrificer all his wishes.

Whitney
Translation
  1. O ladle, ascend the all-nourishing earth; stride, O offering spoon,
    unto the atmosphere; O sacrificial spoon, go to the sky (d├нv) in
    company with the sacrificer; with the little spoon (sruv├б) [as]
    calf, milk thou all the teeming, unirritated quarters.
Notes

The mss. in general strangely accent the two vocatives in a and
b on the final syllable; all ours (save Op.s.m.), and all but one or
two of SPP’s, have dhruv├й (-v├б in saс╣Бhit─Б); all ours (save Op.),
and nearly all SPP’s, have upabhс╣Ы╠Бt; all ours тМКsave Bs.тМЛ and most of
SPP’s, however, accent j├║hu correctly in c (but P.I. have j┼л╠Бh┼л,
and M. has j├║h┼л); both editions make the necessary corrections. At the
end, SPP. gives in his text ├бhс╣Ыс╣З─лyam─Бnaс╕е, with the great majority of
his authorities, and with the comm.* Of our mss., only
O.s.m.Op.D.R.p.m. give -naс╕е, while O.p.m.R.s.m. have -n─Бс╕е; the
reading -n─Бс╕е is, in my opinion, decidedly the preferable one; it is
the quarters that kindly make no resistance to being milked. According
to the comm., the adhvaryu, at time of sacrifice, holds the upabhс╣Ыt
in his left hand, and makes oblation with the juh┼л in his right. The
verse (13 + 11: 12 + 11 + 9 = 56) counts as the Anukr. describes it. Its
ritual use was given under the preceding verse. *тМКThe comm. assumes a
very harsh change to the direct address and applies ahс╣Ыс╣З- to the
sacrificer: atha pratyakс╣гavad uktiс╕е: evaс╣Б srugbhir lokatrayam pr─Бpito
yajam─Бnas tvam ahс╣Ыс╣З─лyam─Бnaс╕е.тМЛ

Griffith

Dhruva, ascend thou earth the all sustainer: go thou, O Upa- bhrit, to air’s mid-region. Juhu, go skyward with the sacrificer; go, and with Sruva be thy calf beside thee drain all the swelling unreluctant quarters.

рдзреНрд░реБрд╡реЗреСред рдЖред рд░реЛреТрд╣реТред рдкреГреТрдерд┐реТрд╡реАрдореНред рд╡рд┐реТрд╢реНрд╡рд╜рднреЛреСрдЬрд╕рдореНред рдЕреТрдиреНрддрд░рд┐реСрдХреНрд╖рдореНред рдЙреТрдкреТрд╜рднреГреТрддреНред рдЖред рдХреНрд░реТрдореТрд╕реНрд╡реТред рдЬреБрд╣реБреСред рджреНрдпрд╛рдореНред рдЧреТрдЪреНрдЫреТред рдпрдЬреСрдорд╛рдиреЗрдиред рд╕рд╛реТрдХрдореНред рд╕реНрд░реБреТрд╡реЗрдгреСред рд╡реТрддреНрд╕реЗрдиреСред рджрд┐рд╢рдГреСред рдкреНрд░рд╜рдкреАреСрдирд╛рдГред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдГреСред рдзреБреТрдХреНрд╖реНрд╡реТред рдЕрд╣реГреСрдгреАрдпрдорд╛рдирдГред рек.ремред

Whitney
Translation
  1. By fords they cross the advances (prav├бt) called the great ones, by
    what [road] the sacrifice-makers, the well-doers, go; there did they
    set a world for the sacrificer, when they arranged the quarters, the
    creatures (bh┼лt├б).

Griffith

They ford the mighty rivers by the pathway which they who sacrifice, the righteous, travel. There they gave room unto the sacrificer when they made regions and existing creatures.

Translation
  1. The track (├бyana) of the An╠Дgirases is the eastern fire; the
    ─Аdityas’ track is the householder’s fire; the track of the sacrificial
    gifts is the southern fire; do thou, with thy limbs, whole (s├бrva),
    powerful (? ┼Ыagm├б), go unto the greatness of Agni [as] disposed by
    br├бhman.
Notes

Both in this verse and in the next, most of our mss. accent falsely
d├бkс╣гiс╣З─Бgnis; SPP. reports it of only one of his, and only in vs. 9.
The comm. glosses ┼Ыagma with sukhita. The verse (11 + 11 + 11: 13 +
11 = 57) counts short of what the Anukr. describes it (ati┼Ыakvar─л = 60
syll.).

Griffith

The Angirases’ pathway is the eastern Agni, the Adityas’ path- way is the Garhapatya: The southward Agni is the way of Southerns. To Agni’s greatness whom the prayer divideth go powerful, un- scathed with all thy members.

режреп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡рд╛ рддрдкрддреБ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Let the eastern fire burn (tap) thee happily (┼Ы├бm) in front; let
    the householder’s fire burn happily behind; let the southern fire burn
    refuge, defense for thee; from the north, from the midst, from the
    atmosphere, from each quarter, O Agni, protect him round about from what
    is terrible.
Notes

тМКCf. vs. 11.тМЛ As to the accent of dakс╣гiс╣З─Бgnis in c, see under vs.
8. The funeral pile is separately, but simultaneously, kindled from each
of the sacrificial fires. To make the verse bhurij, we have to commit
the violence of scanning agne instead of тАШgne in the last p─Бda (so
12 + 10: 12 + 11 + 12 = 57). тМКThe a of agn├нs in a and that of
agne in e are of course to be elided. The insertion of another
tv─Б in b after ┼Ы├бm pa┼Ыc─Б╠Бt rectifies the meter. In c we have
perhaps to tolerate 5 pre-cesural syllables; but with this reservation
and the rectification in b, all 5 p─Бdas are faultless triс╣гс╣нubhs.тМЛ

Griffith

Eastward let east fire happily consume thee, and westward happily the Garhapatya. Burn southern fire, thine armour and protection: from air’s- mid-region from the north and centre, on all sides, Agni, guard thou him from horror.

    with most healthful forms (tan┼л╠Б) carry him that has sacrificed unto
    the heavenly (svarg├б) world, where they revel in common revelry with
    the gods.

Griffith

Do ye, with your most kindly forms, O Agni, waft, turned to rapid steeds whose ribs bear burthens, The sacrificer to the world of Svarga where with the Gods they banquet and are joyful.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Burn (tap), O Agni, happily behind, happily in front; burn him
    happily above, happily below; being one, O J─Бtavedas, triply disposed,
    set him collectedly (samy├бk) in the world of the well-doers.
Notes

тМКCf . vs. 9.тМЛ The adverbs translated ‘behind’ etc. might with at least
equal propriety be rendered ‘on the west,’ ‘on the east,’ ‘on the
north,’ and ‘on the south.’ Nearly all our mss. (not Bs.I.), and half of
SPP’s тМКhave the impossibleтМЛ accent j─Бt├бvedas in c; and a few
(including our O.R.) have at the end lok├бm. тМКAlthough samy├бg enaс╣Б
must pass for the true AV. reading, one cannot forbear to query whether
it has not displaced an original samy├бk t├бс╣Б.тМЛ

Griffith

Happily from the rear burn this man, Agni, happily from before, above, and under. One, triply parted, Jatavedas, place him happily in the world that holds the righteous.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let the fires, kindled, take hold happily; let the J─Бtavedases,
    making done (┼Ыс╣Ыt├б) here him that is Praj─Бpati’s [and] sacrificial,
    not throw him down.
Notes

The verse (11 + 12: 12) lacks a syllable of counting as a full bс╣Ыhat─л.
Two of our mss. (O.R.) read in b j─Бtavedaс╕е (without accent). The
comm. reads sam instead of ┼Ыam at the beginning. тМКCf. vs. 13.тМЛ

тМКThe verse reminds us strongly of 2. 4 (which see), where cikс╣гipas
without ava has quite a different meaning. Here, cikс╣гipan with ava
means ’let them [the fires, not] throw [any part of the dead man]
down’; that is, Agni (in his kindly forms, ┼Ыiv─Б╠Бs tanv├аs) is to treat
the dead man kindly and not let a foot, the head, or a hand fall off
from the funeral pile, but is to consume him completely: cf. the comm.,
who aptly says, yath─Б nirava┼Ыeс╣гaс╣Б dahyate tath─Б. The importance, in
Hindu belief, of having every member of the body carried by Agni to the
other world for use in the next life is abundantly shown by the hymns:
see especially AV. xviii. 3. 9 ab; 2. 24 c; 4. 64; iv. 34. 2: and
Whitney, Oriental and Linguistic Studies, i. 56-57.тАФWhen, as often
happens, the pile of wood is too short for the corpse, the feet will
naturally overhang and drop off from the pyre. In my journal of a visit
at Benares, under date of Feb. 25, 1889, I find the following: “Saw a
cremation, at the Burning Ghat. One foot of the corpse fell off the pyre
(which was none too long), and a man tried to put it back on the fire
with a bamboo. But failing, he took it by the toe with thumb and fingers
and chucked it back.” An allusion to an occurrence of this kind is
clearly made by the Ch─Бndogya Upanishad at vii. 15. 3: atha yady apy
en─Бn utkr─Бntapr─Бс╣З─Б├▒ cch┼лlena [cf. the bamboo, above] sam─Бsaс╣Б
vyatisaс╣Бdahet: n─Бi тАЩv─Бi тАЩnam br┼лyuс╕е pitс╣Ыha тАЩs─л тАЩti etc.тМЛ

Griffith

Happily lit, let fires, each Jatavedas, seize on Prajapati’s appoint- ed victim. Let them not cast it down while here they cook it.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The sacrifice goes, extended, adapting itself (? kс╕╖p), [taking]
    him who hath sacrificed, unto the heavenly (svarg├б) world; let the
    fires enjoy it, made a whole oblation; let the J─Бtavedases, making done
    here him that is Praj─Бpati’s [and] sacrificial, not throw him down.
Notes

in c,тМЛ all refer, of course, to the deceased himself. тМКCf. Whitney,
Oriental and Linguistic Studies, i. 56: “To burn the body of a deceased
person was accordingly an act of solemn sacrifice, which made Agni its
bearer to the other world, the future dwelling of its former
possessor."тАФCf. also Caland’s most apposite citation from B─Бudh─Бyana,
j─Бtasaс╣Бsk─Бreс╣Зe тАЩmaс╣Б lokam abhijayati; mс╣Ыtasaс╣Бsk─Бreс╣З─Б тАЩmuс╣Б lokam, in
his Todtengebr├дuche, pages 174, 178.тМЛ The defective meter and
incomplete construction of b make it altogether probable that the text
is corrupt: ─лj─Бn─Б╠Бn─Бm would help both. The comm. makes no difficulty of
taking abhi..eti causatively, = abhigamayati. He paraphrases
kalp├бm─Бnas by iс╣гс╣нam prade┼Ыam pr─Бpayituс╣Б samarthaс╕е. The mss. vary
between kalp├бm─Бnas, k├бlpam─Бnas, and kalpam─Б╠Бnas; all of ours that
were collated before printing had kalp├б-, which we accordingly
admitted in our text; but we ought to have emended to k├бlpa-, which
SPP. reads. Two of our mss. (O.R.), and one of SPP’s, also have
j─Бtavedasaс╕е at end of d. The verse counts just a full ati┼Ыakvar─л
(11 + 10: 11 + 12: 12 = 56).

Griffith

Sacrifice, duly offered, comes preparing the sacrificer for the. world of Svarga, Let all the fires, each Jatavedas, welcome Prajapati’s completely offered victim. Let them not cast it down while here they cook it.

Whitney
Translation
  1. He that hath sacrificed hath ascended the piled fire, about to fly
    up to heaven (d├нv) from the back of the firmament (n─Б╠Бka); for him,
    the well-doer, shines forth from the welkin (n├бbhas), full of light,
    the heavenly road, traveled by the gods.
Notes

The mss. vary in a between cit├бm and citt├бm; our text reads the
latter; SPP’s the former, which is doubtless correct, and which is
implied by the translation. The comm. notes that agni is used to mean
iс╣гс╣нakacitaс╕е prade┼Ыaс╕е, quoting ─Аpast. 25. 4 as authority. According to
K─Бu┼Ы. (80. 52), the verse (the comm. says, vss. 14-15) accompanies the
laying of the body supine on the pile; it comes next after 1. 46.

Griffith

Fain to fly up from the sky’s ridge to heaven, the worshipper hath mounted visible Agni. Lucid from out the mist to him, the pious, gleams the God- travelled path that leads to Svarga.

Translation

    the right thy supervising priest (brahm├бn); this offered sacrifice,
    being completed (s├бс╣Бsthita), goeth where is the ancient track of those
    offered.

Griffith

On thy right hand let Indra be thy Brahman, Brihaspati Adh- varyu Agni Hotar. This ordered sacrifice goes offered thither whither presented gifts have gone aforetime.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Rich in cakes, rich in milk (kс╣г─лr├б-) let the dish (car├║) take
    seat here; to the world-makers, the road-makers, do we sacrifice,
    whoever of you are here, sharing in the oblation of the gods.
Notes

тМКThe definition of verses 16-24 as 14: 12 + 11 = 37 is right by
mechanical count; but the metrical character of what precedes the first
avas─Бna is wholly misprized by the Anukr.: car├║r ─Б╠Б ih├б s─лdatu is
doubtless an anuс╣гс╣нubh p─Бda; and I am strongly tempted to suspect the
loss (by haplography again: cf. iv. 5. 5, note) of a ca before caru,
poor as the resulting cadence may be, so that instead of 14 we should
have 8 + 8.тМЛ

We had the same refrain above, in 3. 25-35. тМКCf. my introduction to hymn
3, p. 847, ┬╢8.тМЛ According to K─Бu┼Ы. (86. 3), the verses beginning with
ap┼лpav─Бn (16-24) are used as, in each case, what is specified in the
verse (mantroktam) is deposited in the quarters and intermediate
quarters (dikс╣гv aс╣гс╣нamade┼Ыeс╣гu); this is in the ceremony of interment of
the bone-relics, next after the use of 4. 57 and 3. 72 (see under the
latter). тМКAt this point Whitney compares TA. vi. 8 and cites part of it.
The TA. leaves out the depositions in the intermediate directions, SE.
etc., and so has only 5 deposition-mantras instead of 9. The matter is
treated more fully just below.тМЛ According to the comm., caru means
specifically the contents of the dish here: kumbhy─Бm pakva odanaс╕е; and
ih├б signifies: asmin saс╣Бcayanakarmaс╣Зy asthn─Бс╣Б sam─лpe
pa┼Ыcimadigbh─Бge; the others are set in the remaining half-directions,
and one in the middle. тМКObserve that the AV. begins the depositions with
the west (so the comm., at p. 197тБ╕, and at 201┬╣тБ╢ just cited), while the
TA. begins, as noted below, with the east.тМЛ

тМКAs part of the requisites for performing the pitс╣Ыnidh─Бna, K─Бu┼Ы. (83.
2) prescribes eleven dishes (car┼лn). According to K─Бu┼Ы. 86. 2, two
dishes (car┼л*) are to be deposited, with our 4. 57 and 3. 72, near
the head of the human figure formed with the bones (note to 3. 25);
next, eight more (K─Бu┼Ы. 86. 3) in the eight directions, with 8 vss. of
our present sequence, that is, 4. 16-23; and then the eleventh and last
dish in the center with our 4. 24, according to K─Бu┼Ы. 86. 4, where we
are to read (see under vs. 24) madhye тАШpavantam (for pacantam), ‘in
the center [a dish] with water.’тМЛ *тМКSo we must read, with three of
Bloomfield’s mss., as Caland suggests, Todtengebr├дuche, p. 152, and as
the AV. comm. makes plain at 224┬╣тБ╣ (carudvayam), though not at 176┬▓┬│.тМЛ

тМКTA. vi. 8 reads thus: ap┼лp├бv─Бn ghс╣Ыt├бv─Бс╣Е┼Ы car├║r ├й тАШh├б s─лdat┼л
тАЩttabhnuv├бn pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Бс╣Б dy─Б╠Бm ut├│ тАЩp├бri: yonikс╣Ы╠Бtaс╕е pathikс╣Ы╠Бtaс╕е saparyata y├й

тАШs─Бu: d├б┼Ы─Бkс╣гar─Б [:] t─Б╠Бm rakс╣гasva etc. etc.тАФThis set of mantras is
metrical as far as gс╣Ыh├й inclusive, 7 (8?) + 8 + 12: 12 + 11: 8 + 8;
then prose. It accompanies the deposition of the cakes with a dish of

Griffith

Enriched with cake and milk here let the Charu rest. World-makers, makers of the path we worship you of the Gods who here partake oblations.

Translation
  1. The drop leaped (skand) toward the earth, the sky (d├нv), toward
    both this lair (y├│ni) and the one that was of old; of the drop that
    goes about toward the same lair do I make oblation, after seven
    invocations (h├│tr─Б).
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 17. 11, and found also in several other texts: VS.
(xiii. 5), TS. (iv. 2. 8┬▓, 9тБ╡), TA. (vi. 6. 1), MS. (ii. 5. 10), ┼ЫB.
(vii. 4. 1┬▓тБ░). RV. differs from our text by reading in a pratham─Б╠Бс╣Е
├бnu dy┼л╠Бn; all the rest agree throughout with AV., save that TS.TA. have
tс╣Ыt─л╠Бyam for sam─Бn├бm in c. тМКIn MS. this verse stands between our
ix. 4. 5 and 4. 4, as already noted under ix. 4. 5.тМЛ K─Бu┼Ы. does not
apply the verse, but it is found (as above) in the funeral ceremony of
TA., next after our 4. 35 below, being addressed to any overflow of the
offered dish of curds and honey. The comm. explains drapsa by
somarasasthitodakakaс╣Зa, and teaches that such a drop, or the soma
itself, is here praised, in view of the enjoyment of the fruit of their
soma-sacrifices by the Fathers in heaven; it also points out that in CB.
(vii. 4. 1┬▓тБ░) this drop is praised as the sun (─Бditya). In V─Бit. (16.
17) the verse (with RV. x. 17. 12, 13 and one or two others) is used in
the agniс╣гс╣нoma ceremony, with offerings to the soma-drops (v─Бipruс╣гa),
on occasion of the overflow of soma.

Griffith

On all the earth, to heaven, the drop descended, on this place and on that which was before it. I offer up, throughout the seven oblations, the drop which still to one same place is moving.

Whitney
Translation
  1. A hundred-streamed V─Бyu, a heaven-finding sun (? ark├б), wealth, do
    those men-beholders look upon; whoso bestow (pс╣Ы) and present
    (prayam) always, they milk a sacrificial gift having seven mothers.
Notes

The verse corresponds to RV. x. 107. 4, which differs by reading hav├нs
at end of b, тМКand saс╣Бgam├й at end of cтМЛ; it also reads duhate
in d and puts the word after d├бkс╣гiс╣З─Бm; the RV. hymn is one in
praise of generous givers. Nс╣Ыc├бkс╣гasas in b might of course be gen.
sing. (so Grassmann); both translators тМКGrassmann and LudwigтМЛ take
sapt├бm─Бtaram as ‘mother of seven,’ which is against the accent; the
comm. takes it properly as possessive, but gives three different guesses
at its value. The comm. takes t├й in b as ‘for thy sake,’ against
the accent. K─Бu┼Ы. does not quote the verse; the comm. says that it and
the next are used together on watering the bone-relics with water
falling from a vessel with a hundred holes; and these hundred holes it
regards as referred to by the first word of the verse.

Griffith

Those who observe men look on wealth as Vayu with countless. streams, and as light-finding Arka; Those drain out Guerdon sprung from seven mothers, who satis- fy and evermore give presents.

    [as] milch-cow rich in honey, in order to well-being; reveling

    highest firmament (vy├▓man).

Griffith

They for their weal drain out the cask, the beaker four-holed,. the milch-cow Ida full of sweetness, Injure not, Agni, in the loftiest heaven Aditi heightening strength among the people.

рейрез рдПрддрддреНрддреЗ рджреЗрд╡рдГрд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. This garment god Savitar gives thee to wear (bhс╣Ы); putting on
    that, which is t─Бrpy├а, do thou go about in Yama’s realm.
Notes

Some of the mss. (including our O.Op.R.) read dad─Бtu in b. Our Op.
accents t─Б╠Бrpyam, and the word is variously accented by half of SPP’s
authorities. The comm. first explains the word as tarpaс╣З─Бrham
pr─лtikaram, and then adds: ‘or, made of a kind of grass called tс╣Ыp─Б,
[and] anointed with ghee.’ For the ritual use of the verse, in company
with 2. 57, see under the latter verse. The comm. says only that it is
addressed to the garment when the dead man is wrapped up.

Griffith

On thee doth Savitar the God bestow this vesture for thy wear. Clothe thee herein, and find meet robe in Yama’s realm to cover thee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The grains became a milch-cow; the sesame became her calf; upon her,
    unexhausted, one lives in Yama’s realm.
Notes

The mss. are a little at variance as to the accent of tilo тАШbhavat;
but the majority give til├▓, which is accepted in both editions. The
comm. reads at the end j─лv─Бti. The ritual application of this verse
and its successor was given with that of 3. 69 above; the comm. says
here that with vss. 32-34 grains mingled with sesame are put upon the
bones. The first p─Бda is one syllable short.

Griffith

The grains of corn have now become a cow, the Sesamum her calf. He in the realm of Yama lives on her the inexhaustible.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Be these, O so-and-so, thy milch-kine that yield what is desired;
    variegated, white, of like form, of different form, with sesame as calf,
    let them wait upon (upa-sth─Б) thee there.
Notes

One of our mss. (Op.), and three or four of SPP’s authorities, accent
t├нlavats─Бs in d. The comm. has bhavanti in b. The verse (8 +
7: 11 + 11 = 37) is not at all an upariс╣гс╣н─Бdbс╣Ыhat─л, but rather an
irregular ─Бst─Бrapan╠Дkti.

Griffith

Let these become thy milch-kine, man! supplying all thy heart’s desires. There, speckled, white, like-hued and various-coloured, with calves of Sesamum let them stand beside thee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Grains variegated, yellow, white, grains black, red, [be] thy
    milch-kine here; with sesame as calf, yielding (duh) him refreshment,
    be they ever unresisting.
Notes

The verse is found also in TA. (in vi. 7. 1), with its first half
abbreviated to ├йс╣З─лr dh─Бn─Б╠Б h├бriс╣З─лr ├бrjun─лс╕е santu dhen├бvaс╕е; and it
accents t├нla- in c (with our Op. and one or two of SPP’s mss.).
Our O. тМКand apparently also P.I.тМЛ, with тМКone orтМЛ two of SPP’s mss., also
accent en─л╠Бs. Only a minority of the mss. (including our Bs.p.m. and
Op.) have at the end -nt─лс╕е, the rest -nt─л. Here and in vs. 36, most
of the mss. accent anapasph├║r-, and accordingly both edited texts
accept it; but the readings ought unquestionably to be emended to
├бnapasphur- (which is given here by тМКTA., Poona ed.,тМЛ our O.R., тМКand
one or two of SPP’s mss.тМЛ; in 36, by none); the accentuation in this
part of the text is more than usually faulty. The comm. stupidly
declares apasphuraс╣Зa = n─Б┼Ыa, and the participle therefore =
тМКavina┼Ыvaryaс╕е orтМЛ akс╣г─лс╣З─Бс╕е. тМКAs alternative rendering, W. suggests
’not refractory.’тМЛ тМКW’s ‘here’ seems to be meant as (the hardly licit)
version of the accentless asya: Weber notices the wild incongruity
(absent in the TA. version) between asya in a, te in b, and
asm─Б├н in c.тМЛ

Griffith

Let the green grains become thy white, and speckled, The dusky corns become thy ruddy milch-kine. Let those with calves of Sesamum for ever yield strength to him and never flinch from milking.

That is, with fatness or abundance (pinv). The verse is found also at
the beginning of TA. vi. 6; but this rectifies the meter of b by
reading s─Бhasr├бm ├║tsaс╣Б ┼Ыat├бdh─Бram et├бm; and its c, d are not less
different: t├бsminn eс╣г├б pit├бram pit├бmah├бm pr├бpit─Бmaham bibharat

(as noticed above) the verse is next followed by our 4. 28, in the
relic-interment ceremony; according to K─Бu┼Ы. (82. 22), it is used on the
second day after cremation, with an oblation on the back of a
v─Бnyavats─Б* cow, after causing her to be milked on the site of the
funeral pile. The comm. тМКp. 209┬╣тБ╕тМЛ calls the cow anyavats─Б (only by an
error of the editor?). тМКIf error, it is an easy one, for the comm’s
words as combined are dahanasth─Бnasaс╣Бnidh─Бv anyavats─Бy─Бс╕е: but
anyavats─Б occurs in the comm. to AB. vii. 2, mentioned below.тМЛ The
verse (11 + 9: 11 + 12 = 43) is hardly fit to be reckoned a triс╣гс╣нubh.

*тМКPrimarily, v─Бny├а, abhiv─Бny├а, apiv─Бny├а, niv─Бny├а, as gerundives of
van, mean ’to be won over to or wonted to’: abhiv─Бnyavats├б is ‘a
calf that has to be wonted to’ its new or adoptive mother. Such a word
as the last, with bahuvr─лhi accent, means ‘(a cow) possessing such a
calf,’ and by inference, ‘a cow that has lost her own calf’: so
abhiv─Бny├аvats─Б, AB. vii. 2, and Hiraс╣Зyake┼Ыi-s┼лtra, in Caland’s
Pitс╣Ыmedha-s┼лtras, p. 58тБ╕; apiv─Бny├аvats─Б, K─Бu┼Ы., twice?, see below;
niv─Бny├аvats─Б, ┼ЫB. xii. 5. 1тБ┤.тАФThese possessives are then abbreviated,
and we find abhiv─Бny├а at TB. i. 6. 8тБ┤ and four times in the
Pitс╣Ыmedhas┼лtras (see Caland’s Index), and niv─Бny─Б╠А at ┼ЫB. ii. 6. 1тБ╢,
both words with the same meaning as abhiv─Бny├аvats─Б, but coming to it
secondarily; and also v─Бny─Б╠А at TB. ii. 6. 16┬▓, p. 676 Poona, glossed
by mс╣Ыtavats─Б dhenuс╕е, and ─Аp┼ЫS. viii. 15. 17, as equivalent of the not
quotable v─Бny├аvats─Б.тАФAfter putting to paper the explanations just
given I find them confirmed by N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa, to whom I was brought by
Aufrecht’s valuable note upon his excerpt from S─Бyaс╣Зa’s comment on AB.
vii. 2 (p. 377): N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa, in his comm. on A┼ЫS. iii. 10. 17 says
abhiv─Бnyavats─Б n─Бm─Б тАЩnyavatsena dohan─лy─Б: abhiv─Бnyo vatso yasy─Бс╕е s─Б
тАЩbhiv─Бnyavats─Б: abhiv─Бnyo тАШbhivanan─лya ity arthaс╕е.тАФIn K─Бu┼Ы. 82. 22
there can be little doubt (cf. BR. i. 347) that we have to read
apiv─Бnyavats─Бm after ─Бdahane ca; and in like manner, at 80. 25,
apiv─Бnyavats─Бy─Бs: with the latter passage is to be compared ┼ЫB. ii. 6.
1тБ╢, which describes the same ceremony; see also Caland,
Todtengebr├дuche, p. 151. The use of the milk of a cow whose calf is
dead is in keeping with the use of cows that are old, ugly, barren,
etc.: cf. ┼ЫB. xii. 5. 1тБ┤ (dead man’s agnihotra) and Caland, l.c., p.
173, p. 20.тМЛ

Griffith

I offer in Vaisvanara this oblation, thousandfold spring that pours a hundred steamlets. This with a swelling flow supports the Father, supports grand- fathers and their sires before them.

Whitney
Translation
  1. A thousand-streamed, hundred-streamed fountain, unexhausted,
    expanded upon the back of the sea, yielding refreshment, unresisting, do
    the Fathers wait on at their will (? svadh─Б╠Бbhis).

Griffith

Beside the spring with hundred, thousand currents, expanding on the summit of the water, Exhaustless, yielding strength, never reluctant, the Fathers with their sacred food are seated.

Translation
  1. This funeral pile (? k├бs─Бmbu) [is] piled with piling; come, ye
    [his] fellows, look down at it; this mortal goeth to immortality; make
    ye houses for him according to his kindred.

A number of the mss. (including our P.M.I.) read in a citt├бm, as
in 14 a above. The pada-text at end of b is pa┼Ыyata: ─Б╠Б: ita.

its usual skill in explaining kas─Бmbu; it means kas─Б┼Ы c─Б тАЩmb┼лni ca,
kasa being by abbreviation from k─лkasa, and = asthi! K─Бu┼Ы. (86. 1)
has the verse accompany the viewing of the bone-relics тМКwhich are now in
the trench, says Ke┼Ы.тМЛ by the ‘fellows’ of the deceased; the comm. says
that either the relatives or all are to look at them as deposited in the
hollow, while the manager recites the verse. The meter of the last p─Бda

Griffith

This pile of wood, collected, heaped together, regard it, O ye, kinsmen, and come near it. To immortality this mortal goeth: prepare a home for him, all ye his kindred.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЗрджрдореН) рдпрд╣ (рдХрд╕рд╛рдореНрдмреБ)рд╢рд╛рд╕рди рдХрд╛ рдХреАрд░реНрддрди (рдЪрдпрдиреЗрди) рдЗрдХрдЯреНрдард╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ (рдЪрд┐рддрдореН) рдЗрдХрдЯреНрдард╛ рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рдЧрдпрд╛ рд╣реИ, (рд╕рдЬрд╛рддрд╛рдГ) рд╣реЗрд╕рдЬрд╛рддрд┐рдпреЛ ! рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Whitney
Translation
  1. Be thou just here, winning riches, with thought here, with ability
    here; be thou here, very heroic, vigor-bestowing, not smitten away.
Notes

The comm. understands iha citta iha kratuс╕е as four independent words.
According to K─Бu┼Ы. (87. 21), the verse is made to accompany the taking
of one of two lighted sticks of wood (see under 1. 56), and setting it
up in the dirt (see under 2. 34). That this was its original office may
be questioned; perhaps it is rather an invocation of the ancestor for
help to his descendants.

Griffith

Be here, even here, acquiring wealth, here be thou thoughts here be thou strength. Be stronger here in manly power, life-giver, never beaten back.

Griffith

Giving the son and grandson satisfaction, let these the present Waters full of sweetness, Pouring forth food and Amrit for the Fathers, refresh both these and those, the Goddess Waters.

рекреж рдЖрдкреЛ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. O waters, send forth (pra-hi) Agni unto the Fathers; this
    sacrifice of mine let the Fathers enjoy; they who attach themselves unto
    a sitting refreshment, may they confirm to us wealth having all heroes.
Notes

A corresponding verse is found in HGS. (in ii. 10. 6), reading thus:
─Бpo dev─лс╕е pra hiс╣Зut─Б тАЩgnim etaс╣Б yaj├▒am pitaro no juс╣гant─Бm: m─Бs─л тАЩm─Бm
┼лrjam uta ye bhajante te no rayiс╣Б sarvav─лraс╣Б ni yacchantu; and the
comparison appears to convict our unintelligible third p─Бda of being a
very gross corruption. тМКObserve that the word preceding ─Бs─лnam ends in
m, and cf. the cases assembled under xviii. 2. 3.тМЛ The comm. has no
difficulty in explaining ‘a sitting refreshment’ as “a piс╣Зс╕Нa set upon
the barhis.” Both editions read at the end yach─Бn, but all the mss.
save one of SPP’s read yach─Бt; the comm. has -─Бn. The Anukr. does
not heed that the first p─Бda is jagat─л. For the ritual application,
see under the preceding verse. тМКWith a, cf. 2. 4 d, above.тМЛ

Griffith

Waters, send Agni forward to the Fathers: let them accept the sacrifice I offer. May they who follow Vigour that abideth there send us down wealth with full store of heroes.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖрдкрдГ) рд╣реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп [рдЧреМрдУ !] (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ [рдкреНрд░рддрд╛рдк рд╡рд╛ рдмрд▓] рдХреЛ (рдкрд┐рддреДрдиреН рдЙрдк) рдкрд┐рддрд░реЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рдкреНрд░рд╣рд┐рдгреБрдд) рдмрдврд╝рд╛рдпреЗ рдЬрд╛рдУ, (рдореЗ) рдореЗрд░реЗ (рдЗрдордореН) рдЗрд╕ (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН) рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХреЛ (рдкрд┐рддрд░рдГ) рдкрд┐рддрд░ рд▓реЛрдЧ (рдЬреБрд╖рдиреНрддрд╛рдореН) рд╕реЗрд╡рди рдХрд░реЗрдВред (рдпреЗ) рдЬреЛ [рдкрд┐рддрд░ рд▓реЛрдЧ] (рдЖрд╕реАрдирд╛рдореН) рдЙрдкрд╕реНрдерд┐рдд (рдКрд░реНрдЬрдореН) рдмрд▓рдХрд╛рд░рдХрд░рд╕ [рджреВрдз рдШреА рдЖрджрд┐] рдХреЛ (рдЙрдк) рдЖрджрд░ рд╕реЗ (рд╕рдЪрдиреНрддреЗ) рд╕реЗрд╡реЗрдВ, (рддреЗ) рд╡реЗ [рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкрд┐рддрд░] (рдирдГ)рд╣рдореЗрдВ (рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡реАрд░рдореН) рдкреВрд░реЗ рд╡реАрд░ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рд░рдпрд┐рдореН) рдзрди (рдирд┐) рдирд┐рдпрдо рд╕реЗ (рдпрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдиреН) рджреЗрд╡реЗрдВреерекрежрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Whitney
Translation
  1. They kindle the immortal one, oblation-carrying, ghee-loving; he
    knoweth the deposited deposits, the Fathers that are gone away to the
    distances.
Notes

The comm., with his usual disregard of the accent, takes ghс╣Ыtapr├нyam
as from ghс╣Ыt├б + priy├б тМКpr─лtikaram ─Бjyaс╣Б yasyaтМЛ. For the ritual use
as prescribed by K─Бu┼Ы. 87. 22, see under 2. 34, one of the verses that
accompanies it. But the verse is used also, by K─Бu┼Ы. 86. 18, at the end
of the ceremony of interment on “making the devouring (saс╣Бkasuka) fire
blaze up”; this the comm. does not report in his statement of viniyoga.
тМКCaland appears to be right in thinking that the prat─лka samindhate
means samindhate saс╣Бkasukam, xii. 2. 11, and not our verse here. See
under xii. 2. 11 and note the free use of vss. from xii. 2. in the
s┼лtras immediately following 86. 18.тМЛ

Griffith

Lover of butter, deathless, him, Oblation-bearer, they inflame. He knoweth well the treasured stores gone to the Fathers, far away.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What stirabout for thee, what rice-dish, what flesh I offer
    (ni-pс╣Ы) to thee, be they for thee rich in svadh─Б╠Б, rich in honey,
    dripping with ghee.
Notes

The second half-verse is identical with 3. 68 c, d, above. Nearly
all the mss. (of ours, all save Op.) accent m├бntham in a; both
editions read manth├бm. The comm. again тМКsee under 2. 30тМЛ notes the
technical sense of ni-pс╣Ы: niparaс╣Зaс╣Б n─Бma pitryopav─лtin─Б par─Бc─лnap─Бс╣Зin─Б
pitrarthaс╣Б coditadravyasya prakс╣гepaс╕е. By K─Бu┼Ы. 84. 6, the verse
accompanies an offering of the articles mentioned, in the hut (vimita)
in the preparation for interment of the relics; the comm. overlooks
this. тМКFor the ceremony, cf. Caland, Todtengebr├дuche, p. 137.тМЛ

Griffith

The mingled draught, the mess of rice, the flesh which I present to thee, May these be full of food for thee, distilling fatness, rich in sweets.

Translation
  1. What grains I scatter along for thee, mixed with sesame, rich in
    svadh─Б╠Б, be they for thee abundant, prevailing; them let king Yama
    approve for thee.
Notes

This is a repetition of 3. 69, being distinguished as such (and not of
4. 26) by the words ├нti p┼л╠Бrv─Б, instead of ├нty ├йk─Б, after the prat─лka
in most of the mss. Nevertheless, the two saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. of ours (O.R.)
which give it in full, read udbhv─л╠Бs in c, the word in 4. 26,
instead of vibhv─л╠Бs, that in 3. 69; and the comm. also states the
repetition to be of 4. 26; and SPP’s text reads accordingly. тМКFor the
ritual, see under 3. 69.тМЛ

Griffith

Grains which for thee I scatter, mixt with Sesamum as sacred food, May these for thee be excellent and potent. King Yama look on, them, as thine, with favour.

Translation
  1. This [is] the former, the after down-track, by which thy former
    Fathers went away; they who are the forerunners, the followers (?
    abhiс╣г├бc) of it, they carry thee to the world of the well-doing.
Notes

Our reading abhiс╣г─Б╠Бcas is an emendation, almost every ms. giving
abhi┼Ы─Б╠Бcas (our Op. has abhiре░s─Б╠Бcaс╕е, and also one тМКor twoтМЛ of SPP’s
authorities); -с╣г─Б╠Бc- is of course intended, and the comm. gives it.
SPP’s text follows the mss. The comm. explains niy─Бna as the wagon
(┼Ыakaс╣нa) on which the corpse is carried to the funeral pile; and the
‘forerunners’ and ‘followers’ as the oxen that draw it, in front and on
all sides: which is doubtless not at all the true sense; he also reads
vahantu in d. The verse is one of the hariс╣З─лs тМКK─Бu┼Ы. 80. 35; 82.
31 noteтМЛ: see under 1. 61. It lacks (in a) a syllable of being a
full triс╣гс╣нubh. Its second p─Бda is identical with 1. 54 b.

Griffith

This is the ancient, this the recent pathway, by which thy sires of olden time departed. They who first travelled it, and they who followed, convey thee to the world where dwell the righteous.

Translation
  1. On Sarasvat─л do the pious call; on Sarasvat─л, while the sacrifice is
    being extended; on Sarasvat─л do the well-doers call; may Sarasvat─л give

Notes
Griffith

The pious call Sarasvati: they worship Sarasvati while sacrifice proceedeth. The righteous doers of good deeds invoke her: Sarasvati send bliss to him who giveth!

Translation
  1. On Sarasvat─л do the Fathers call, arriving at the sacrifice on the
    south; sitting on this barh├нs, do ye revel; assign thou to us food
    free from disease.
Notes
Griffith

Approaching on the south our solemn worship, the Fathers call- Sarasvati to hear them. Sit on this holy grass and be ye joyful: give thou us strengthen- ing food that brings no sickness.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thee, being earth, I make enter into earth; may god Dh─Бtar lengthen
    out our life-time; let him that goeth very far away be a finder of good
    for you; then may the dead (pl.) come to be (sam-bh┼л) among the
    Fathers.
Notes

The first p─Бda is identical with that of xii. 3. 22, and hence the comm.
here makes the blunder of reporting this verse as quoted by K─Бu┼Ы. 61.
30,* whereas it is evidently the other; and he explains the meaning to
be that earth is smeared upon the vessel тМКporridge-potтМЛ, which is
entirely out of place in this connection, the analogy being with our own
phrase “earth to earth.” The problematic p├бr─Бpar─Бit─Б тМКp.
p├бr─Бре░par─Бit─БтМЛ in c is rendered strictly according to its form, as
if composed of p├бr─Б-par─Б+etс╣Ы; the Pet. Lexx. render it as “one who
departs after another or in due order”; but I cannot see how this
meaning is arrived at. The comm. reads par─Бparet─Бs (our O. gives
-retas), and explains it as d┼лrade┼Ыam par─Бn╠Дmukham ito gat─Бс╕е. The
comm. also, against pada-text and accent, understands adh─Б тАЩmс╣Ыt─Бs in
d. *тМКCf. p. 869, ┬╢7.тМЛ

Griffith

As Prithivi rests on earth, so do I seat thee. May the God Dhatar lengthen our existence. For you may he who parts in turn find treasures, but let the Dead among the Fathers.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Start ye (du.) forward hither, wipe off that which the portents (?
    abhibh─Б╠Б) have said there of you; from that come ye, inviolable ones,
    to this which is better, being bestowers here on me, a giver to the
    Fathers.
Notes

This is highly obscure, and the second half-verse, especially, is
rendered only mechanically, and even then with substitution of v├бs─лyas
where nearly all the mss. have v├б┼Ы─лyas or va┼Ы─лyas (our M.I.D., and
one of SPP’s, va┼Ы─Бyas, which our text, quite unsuccessfully, emends to
va┼Ы─Б╠Бya); SPP. admits v├б┼Ы─лyas in his text; the comm. has v├бs─лyas.
According to K─Бu┼Ы. (82. 40), the verse is addressed to the two kine (the
comm. says, the two that have drawn the hearse): the direction is iti
g─Бv─Бv upayachati; it is perhaps intended as a purification of them
after the ill-omened service which they have performed. In c the
vocative, aghny─Бu, is an emendation, SPP. reading with the mss.
aghny─Б├║; but the accentuation of the mss. is here very
unauthoritative; the comm. also takes the word as vocative. Nearly all
our mss. (all save O.Op.R.) leave ┼лcus in b without accent. The
comm. is not ashamed to derive abhibh─Бs formally from abhi-bh┼л, and
to explain it by abhibh─Бvak─Бs or d┼лс╣гak─Бs; his general explication of
the p─Бda, as intimating a reproach brought against the pair for having
been engaged in such business, is doubtless good. The defective meter
suggests a corruption of the text. The comm. takes iha and bhojan─Бu
in d as two independent words, and renders bhojan─Бu by
bhojayit─Бr─Бu or p─Бlayit─Бr─Бu. Two of SPP’s mss. also accent the words
separately. тМКOn his margin Whitney pencilled the memorandum, “Recast
this note."тМЛ тМКIn Ppp., immediately after our xvii. 1. 30, comes this
verse. Its appearance in that place is possibly to be interpreted as a
hint at the existence in Ppp. of our book xviii., of which, however,
there are no other traces in Ppp. save the straggling verses 1. 46 (in
ii.), 2. 13 (in xix.), 2. 17 and 3. 56 (in xx.).тМЛ тМКтШЮ Last addition
misplaced: see p. 1016.тМЛ

Griffith

Depart ye two: wipe ye away whatever omens of evil fortune here have told you. Go from this man, both Steers, to him who wills it: ye are my joys here by the giver’s Fathers.

Whitney
Translation
  1. This sacrificial gift hath come excellently to us, given by him,
    well-milking, vigor-bestowing; old age, coming close to (? upa-pс╣Ыc)
    them living in youth, shall lead these away together unto the Fathers.
Notes

Griffith

From a good quarter have we gained this guerdon, gift of this man, strength giving, plenteous milker. Bringing in youth old age unto the living, may she bear these together to the Fathers.

Translation
  1. This barh├нs I bring forward for the Fathers; a living, higher one
    I strew for the gods; that do thou ascend, O man, becoming sacrificial;
    let the Fathers acknowledge thee who art departed.
Notes

A corresponding verse is found in TA. (in vi. 7. 2), which reads in
a bharema, for b dev├йbhyo j─л╠Бvanta ├║ttaram bharema, for c,

yamy├а saс╣Бvid─Бn├бс╕е: its text is plainly in part corrupt. Bh├бvan in
c is an emendation, all our mss. save one (Op.), and the majority of
SPP’s, reading bhavan, as if mixing the word up with bhava,
imperative. The comm. reads in b j─лvan. Neither this verse nor its
predecessor is to be called with any reason a jagati; but 50 c, d
and 51 c have jagat─л cadencesтМЛ. This has the same prat─лka, so
far as concerns the first two words, as 1. 46, and it is impossible to
tell which of the two verses is quoted by K─Бu┼Ы.; but the comm. declares
the first half of this one to be used as darbha-grass is strewn upon
the wood of the funeral pile, and the second half as the corpse is laid
supine upon the grass thus strewn: that is to say, this verse is
intended in K─Бu┼Ы. 80. 51; тМКso also Caland, WZKM. viii. 368тМЛ. *тМКThe mss.
vary between bhavaс╣Б and bhava and the TA. comm. understands

I bring this clipped grass hither for the Fathers: grass living,. higher, for the Gods I scatter. Mount this, O man, as victim: let the Fathers recognize thee: when thou hast travelled yonder.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thou hast sat upon this barh├нs, thou hast become sacrificial; let
    the Fathers acknowledge thee who art departed; collect thy body
    according to its joints; I arrange thy members with br├бhman.
Notes

The reading yath─Бpar├║ in c is an emendation, made alike by both
editions;* the comm. has it, but all the mss. give yath─Бpur├║тАФwhich is
perhaps not altogether untranslatable: ‘according to its muchness.’ We
should expect in b rather j─Бnan than another j─Бnatu (51 d).
The verse evidently belongs with its predecessor тМКused at 80. 51тМЛ, but
is entirely separated from it in ritual use, accompanying, according to
K─Бu┼Ы. 85. 25, тМКthe assembling of the bones so as to form a human figure,
as explained under 3. 25тМЛ; next after it are quoted 2. 24, 26 and 3.
25-37. P─Бda b has an extra syllable. тМКWith regard to the place of
the vs., see p. 870, ┬╢1, and p. 870, end.тМЛ

*тМКIn support of the emendation, SPP. adduces ix. 5. 4, with its
yath─Бpar├║ and paru┼Ы├бs. I think that yath─Бpar├║ (as against
yath─Бpur├║) is strongly supported by the sense (much less so by the
mss.) of the two K─Бu┼Ыikan passages which give the ritual for ix. 5. 4
and for this vs. respectively, to wit, 64. 10 and 85. 25. In the latter
passage the mss. have yath─Бparuс╕е saс╣Бcinoti (one, -puru), and Ke┼Ыava
says yath─Бparu, and Bloomfield emends to yath─Бparu; but I am not
quite sure that it is necessary, for yath─Бparus may not be bad
Sanskrit.тМЛ

Griffith

Set on this grass thou hast become a victim. Fathers shall know thee yonder when they meet thee. Gather thy body, limb by limb, together: I by the power of prayer arrange thy members.

Whitney
Translation
  1. King leaf is the cover of the dishes; the strength of refreshment,
    the power, vigor, hath come to us, dispensing (vi-dh─Б) life-time to
    the living (pl.), in order to length of life for a hundred autumns.
Notes

The comm. reads in a, against the pada-text and the metrical
requirement, the later abbreviated pidh─Бnam. It understands by parс╣Зa
(’leaf’) the tree so called, or the pal─Б┼Ыa-tree; and this may be
correct; this tree, it says, owing to its sacrificial quality, is the
overlord of trees. тМКCf. the synonyms brahmap─Бdapa (in Hemacandra) and
y─Бj├▒ika, viprapriy─Б (in R─Бjanighaс╣Зс╣нu): cf. also brahma v─Бi pal─Б┼Ыah,
┼ЫB. xiii. 8. 4┬╣.тМЛ It takes ┼лrj├бs as a nominative, which makes a
decidedly easier reading, but is unsupported by Vedic usage elsewhere.
Only two or three mss. (including our Op.) read in c vid├бdhat, the
rest v├нdadhat (and the pada-mss. v├нре░dadhat, which is absurd тМКcf.
note to xiii. 3. 17тМЛ, but rather indicates that the word was correctly
viewed as a participle); and SPP. accepts v├нdadhat, p. v├нре░dadhat,
because the comm. supports the majority of the mss. by understanding v├н
dadhat. The true reading is, beyond all reasonable question,
vid├бdhat, as our text gives it. The meter seems to be viewed by the
Anukr. as 10 + 11: 8 + 11 = 40; it is rather too irregular to merit a
name. Its use* in K─Бu┼Ы. (86. 6) follows that of vs. 36 above; it
accompanies the laying of middle-foliage (? madhyamapal─Б┼Ы─Бs) down upon
the offering dishes: the comm. says, more explicitly, upon the nine
dishes spoken of in vss. 16-24, and also upon the perforated plates
(madhyapal─Б┼Ыapatr─Бir ─Бcch─Бdayet); Ke┼Ыava’s explanation corresponds
closely with this.

*тМКThe pal─Б┼Ыa has ternate leaves, from 8 to 16 inches long: Roxburgh,
Flora Indica, p. 540, Calc. ed. 1874. By madhyama parс╣Зa or pal─Б┼Ыa
is meant the middle one of any of these ternate groups; the middle one
is especially fit for holy use by reason of its likeness to a
sacrificial ladle: TB. i. 6. 10┬│, madhyam├йna parс╣З├йna juhoti: sr├║g ghy
├ис╣г─Б╠Б: cf. also S─Бyaс╣Зa on TS. i. 8. 6, p. 1167, Poona. I am indebted to
Caland’s excellent paragraphs on this subject, ZDMG. liii. 212.тАФThe
“nine dishes” are the last nine of the eleven whose deposition is
explained above, under vs. 16. The “plates” are the leaky old dishes
noticed above under vs. 36.тМЛ

Griffith

The royal Parna is the caldrons’ cover: strength have we gained, force, power, and might, and vigour. Bestowing length of life upon the living, for long existence through a hundred autumns.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The share of refreshment that generated this man;тАФthe stone attained
    (gam) the overlordship of the foods;тАФhim praise ye, all-befriended,
    with oblations; may that Yama make (dh─Б) us to live further.
Notes

The second half-verse is identical with 3. 63 c, d above. The
translation of the first half is purely mechanical, the sense being
wholly obscure. The comm. renders bh─Бg├бs by sambhakt─Б, and ┼лrj├бs
by annasy─Б тАЩsthisam─лpasth─Бpitacarulakс╣гaс╣Зasya, yamas being the
implied subject; then the ‘stone’ is the one used to cover the same
ann─Бni or caravas. A couple of our mss. (O.R.) and one of SPP’s read
in b ├б┼Ыv─Б╠Б тАЩnn─Бm; several (including our O.Op.R.) have
├бdhipatyam. Some of ours (O.R.K.) and three of SPP’s leave jag─Бma
without an accent, which seems better, and is implied in the
translation. One of SPP’s gives bh─Бg├бm in a. In K─Бu┼Ы. (86. 7) the
verse is used next after 53, and accompanies the covering of the same
dishes with stonesтАФor, the comm. adds, with bricks. тМКCf. Caland,
Todtengebr├дuche, p. 157.тМЛ It lacks a syllable in a. Our edition
leaves vi┼Ыvamitr─Бs in this verse without accent, on the authority of
two of our mss. (Bp.M.); all SPP’s give vi┼Ыv├бmitr─Бs, p.
vi┼Ыv├бре░mitr─Бс╕е, as in 3. 63, and he accepts this in his text. The two
verses ought of course to be made to agree, but there is little reason
for preferring either nominative or vocative тМКthe comm. takes the
doubtful word as voc.тМЛ. тМКIf the Vi┼Ыv─Бmitras be not meant here and at 3.
63, then Weber’s observations reported under 3. 16 lose some of their
basis.тМЛ

Griffith

The share of vigour which gave this man being, the stone won lordship over foods that nourish. Hymn this with your oblations, Visvamitras: may he, may Yama, lengthen our existence.

релрел рдпрдерд╛ рдпрдорд╛рдпрд╣рд░реНрдореНрдпрдорд╡рдкрдиреНрдкрдЮреНрдЪ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. As the five clans (m─Бnav├б) scattered (vap) a dwelling (harmy├б)
    for Yama, so do I scatter a dwelling, that there may be many of me (?).
Notes

A corresponding verse is found in TA. (in vi. 6. 2); it reads h─Бrmy├бm
in a and c, and ev├бm in c; and for d y├бth─Б╠Б тАЩs─Бma
j─лvalok├й bh┼л╠Бrayas, which, however unmetrical, is at least capable of
being translated, while this can hardly be claimed for our d. All
the mss. read at the end ├бsatas, save one of SPP’s, which follows the
comm. in giving ├бsata, as is read in both editionsтАФin ours, purely as
an emendation. The comm. makes no difficulty of taking ├бsata as =
sy─Бta, and explaining “that ye my relatives may be numerous”; but that
would be ├бsatha; and ├бsata has no grammatical standing of any kind,
and hence is to be rejected. The comparison with TA. at least shows that

v─Б u na (xviii. 2. 50) upa sarpa (3. 49) as─Бu h─Б (4 .66) iti
cinvanti. S┼лtra 11 continues: yath─Б yam─Бya (4. 55) iti saс╣Б┼Ыritya.
Upon 10, Ke┼Ы. says: ┼Ыil─Бbhir (? ┼Ыal─Бk─Бbhir?) viс╣гam─Бbhir iс╣гс╣нak─Бbhir
v─Б prasavyaс╣Б cinvanti ┼Ыma┼Ы─Бnam. And the AV. comm., in giving the ritual

kuс╣нс╣нayeyuс╕е.тАФIn all these passages, ┼Ыma┼Ы─Бna or ┼Ыma┼Ы─Бna-de┼Ыa or

praj├▒─Бnaс╣Б v─Б (‘or as a monument’), and Harisv─Бmin’s comment, p. 1017┬╣тБ╡,
┼Ыma┼Ы─Бnam prasiddham asthi-saс╣Бrakс╣гa-v─Бstu; the mound is, as with us,

this be right and if kuс╣нс╣нay is the comm’s version of the word after
iti in s┼лtra 11, then I suspect that Bloomfield has not hit the

meaning of kuс╣нс╣нay and also to the probable intention of Bl’s mss., and
I would accordingly read saс╣Б┼Ыnathya in place of the printed
saс╣Б┼Ыritya. Root ┼Ыnath means ’thrust, push,’ in their ordinary and in
their obscene senses, and here, with sam, ’to make [the mound]
compact or firm by striking or beating or patting,’ as a modern
gravemaker pats the mound with his spade to give it shape and firmness.тМЛ

Griffith

As the Five Races of mankind for Yama set apart a house. Even so I set a house apart that greater numbers may be mine.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Wear (bhс╣Ы) thou this gold, which thy father wore before; of thy
    father, going to heaven (svarg├б), do thou wipe off the right hand.
Notes

The majority of mss. read pitur in c, some p├нtur, and hardly any
(of ours, only Op.) pit├║r. Many of ours have mс╣Ыс╕Нhс╕Нhi in d: see
Pr─Бt. i. 94 and note. The comm. strangely gives pipс╣Ыhi тМКcf. xiii. 1.
1, noteтМЛ in a (though abibhar in b!). According to K─Бu┼Ы. 80.
46, 47, the first half-verse is used as the manager takes with the right
hand some gold worn by the deceased, smears it with ghee, and passes it
to the eldest son; the second half-verse, as he makes him wipe off his
(of course, the father’s) right hand; the comm. states it thus: “with
the first half he makes the oldest son heat (─Бdipayet: as if the comm.
read in K─Бu┼Ы. ─Бd─лpayati instead of ─Бd─Бp-) in the fire gold found in
the hand of the deceased; with the other half the son should wipe the
deceased’s hand.”

Griffith

Take thou and wear this piece of gold, the gold thy father used to wear. Wipe tenderly the right hand of thy sire who goes away to heaven.

Translation
  1. Both those who are living and those who are dead; those who are born
    and those who are worshipfulтАФfor them let there go a brook of ghee,
    honey-streamed, overflowing.
Notes

┼Ыat├бdh─Бr─Б instead of m├бdhudh─Бr─Б. The mss. are again at variance as

jaj├▒iy─Бs, explaining it as jaj├▒im utpattiс╣Б y─Бnti gacchanti: that is,
jaj├▒iтАФroot y─Б! The comm. also understands in d madhudh─Бr─Бs, as
object of vyundat─л. A corresponding verse is found in TA. (in vi. 12):
it omits the first ca in a; has at end of b the almost
acceptable reading j├бnty─Бs (it ought to be j├бntv─Бs); offers in c
the curious corruption dh─Бrayitum for kuly─Бi тАЩtu; тМКand accents

80. 46; the K─Бu┼Ы. uses it twice with 3. 72: see under that verse; in TA.
it has an utterly different application, in the ceremony of turning
loose the cow that was led with the corpse to the funeral pile.

Griffith

To all, the living and the dead, all that are born, the worshipful. Let the full brook of fatness run, o’erflowing, with stream of mead.

Whitney
Translation
  1. There purifies itself the conspicuous bull of the prayers, the sun
    of days, lengthener out of dawns, of the sky (d├нv); the breath of the
    rivers hath made the jars to resound loudly; entering Indra’s heart with
    skill.
Notes

This is a verse out of one of the most formidable hymns of the RV.
soma-book (RV. ix. 86. 19), and occurring also twice in SV. (i. 559; ii.
171). In b, RV. reads s├│mo ├бhnaс╕е pratar─лt├│ тАЩс╣г├бso div├бс╕е; in c,
kr─Бс╣З─Б╠Б and av─лva┼Ыat; in d, h─Б╠Бrdi and man─лс╣г├нbhis; with this
SV. in general agrees, but has, with AV., ├бhn─Бm and uс╣г├бs─Бm in b,
and acikradat in c; it is peculiar in reading pr─Бс╣З─Б╠Б (p.
praре░─Бn─Б╠Б) at beginning of c; a corruption, doubtless, which is
carried out to greater intelligibility in our pr─Бс╣З├бs. The AV.
corruption, of both sense and meter, in b, prat├бr─лt─Б uс╣г-,
supported by the pada-reading praре░t├бr─лt─Бс╕е, is very strange; of our

Griffith

Far-seeing he flows on, the Bull, the Lord of hymns, promoter of the Sun, of Days, of Dawns, of Heaven. Breath of the rivers he hath roared into the jars, and through his wisdom entered into Indra’s heart.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let thy sparkling (? tveс╣г├б) smoke cover, being in the sky,
    extended bright; for thou, O purifier, shinest like the sun with luster,
    with beauty (kс╣Ыp─Б╠Б).
Notes

The verse is RV. vi. 2. 6 and SV. i. 83; both read с╣Ыс╣Зvati in a;
тМКin b, SV. combines div├н s├бс╣Е ch-: cf. div├н с╣г├бс╣Е ch- at xvii. 1.
12тМЛ. The comm. explains kс╣Ыp─Б as = kс╣Ыpay─Б or stuty─Б. V─Бit. (6. 11)
uses the verse, with others, in the ceremony of establishing the fires.

Griffith

Let thy bright smoke envelop thee, spread forth, O Bright One, in the sky. For, Purifier, like the Sun thou shinest with thy radiant glow.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Soma (├нndu) verily goes forward to Indra’s rendezvous; the comrade
    does not violate (pra-m─л) the comrade’s agreements; thou rushest to
    join, as a male after femalesтАФsoma, in the jar, by a road of a hundred
    tracks.
Notes

The verse corresponds to RV. ix. 86. 16, which has, however, important
variants: in a, pr├│ ay─Бs─лd ├нndur and niс╣Ыkс╣Ыt├бm; in b,
saс╣Бg├нram; in c, yuvat├нbhis and arс╣гati; in d, ┼Ыat├бy─Бmn─Б;
SV. (i. 557; ii. 502) agrees with RV. except in the last item, having,
like our text, -y─Бman─Б. тМКThe meter shows that it is to be pronounced
-y─Бman─Б, whichever way it is written: cf. JAOS. x. 532.тМЛ Our
n├нс╣гkс╣Ыtim is hardly better than a corruption of the RV. reading; but
the comm. understands it as Indra’s “belly” (jaс╣нharalakс╣гaс╣З─Бс╣Б sth─Бnam),
and supports his opinion by quoting RV. iii. 35. 6. Saс╣Бgir├бs, in
b, is understood in the translation as saс╣Бg├нras (which is read by
two or three mss., including our O.), the former being unintelligible;
the comm. gives two explanations, both implying the accent -g├нr-, one
from sam-gс╣Ы ‘agree,’ the other from sam-gс╣Ы or -gil ‘swallow down,’
thus finding in the verse another “belly” (saс╣Бgiras = saс╣Бgiram =
udaram). Our text of c spoils both the meter and the connection,
making the line render very lamely; the comm. reads y├│с╣г─Б and takes it
as an instrumental (like yuvat├нbhis); in d he has the RV.SV.
reading. The metrical definition of the Anukr. is worthless. тМКThe RV.
verse is a good jagat─л, and so is this, barring c, where the
corruptions have spoiled meter as well as sense.тМЛ

Griffith

Indu is moving forth to Indra’s destined place, and slights not as a friend the promise of his friend. Thou, Soma, comest nigh as bridegroom meets the bride, reach- ing the beaker by a course of hundred paths.

Whitney
Translation
  1. They have eaten; they have revelled тМКsurelyтМЛ; they have shaken off
    (├бva) those that are dear; having own brightness (sv├бbh─Бnu), they
    have praised; inspired, youngest, we implore.
Notes

The verse corresponds to RV. i. 82. 2 a-d, and is found also in
other texts: SV. i. 415; VS. iii. 51; TS. in i. 8. 5┬▓; MS. in i. 10. 3.
All these agree in reading in c priy─Б╠Бs for priy─Б╠Бn, and, for
d, v├нpr─Б n├бviс╣гс╣нhay─Б mat─л╠Б; and they add a fifth p─Бda, a refrain,
having nothing to do with the meaning of the verse. A majority of the
AV. mss. (including our M.O.Op.R.K.D.) read ├бv─Б тАЩpriy─Б╠Бс╣Е (p. ├бva:
apriy─Б╠Бn), and this is perhaps the true Atharvan text (though the
accent, in that case, should be ├бv─Б╠Б тАЩpriy─Бn), and defensible on the
ground of sense; our last p─Бda is nothing but a senseless corruption. In
K─Бu┼Ы. (88. 27) the verse is used, next after vss. 81 ff.,* in the
piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a, with the direction ity uttarasicam avadh┼лya; the
comm. paraphrases this to mean that one is to perform an additional
sprinkling (? uttarapariс╣гeka) next after the worship (upasth─Бna) of
the piс╣Зс╕Нas. For the application of the verse to the Fathers, compare
TB. ii. 6. 3┬▓, ├бkс╣гan pit├бraс╕е: ├бm─лmadanta pit├бraс╕е, etc.; тМКalso
S─Бyaс╣Зa’s comm. on TS. i. 8. 5┬▓, Poona ed., p. 1159тМЛ. *тМКIt is to be
noted that in the piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a of the VS. (ii. 31), am─лmadanta
pitaraс╕е etc. comes just before the verses corresponding to our vss.
81-85.тМЛ тМК┼ЫGS., i. 15, prescribes the RV. verse for use when the bride
greases the axle of the wedding-car: is this because of the resemblance
of akс╣гam (‘axle’) to akс╣гan (root ghas)?!тМЛ тМКSee p. lxxix.тМЛ

Griffith

Well have they eaten and rejoiced: their dear ones have they shaken off. Sages, self-luminous, have praised: we who are youngest supplicate.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Come ye, O Fathers, delectable, by profound roads that the Fathers
    travel, assigning to us lifetime and progeny; and do ye attach
    yourselves to us with abundances of wealth.
Notes

The last p─Бda was found above as ix. 4. 24 d. Corresponding verses
are found in HGS. ii. 10. 5 and MB. ii. 3. 5. For a, b, MB. reads
eta pitaraс╕е somy─Бso gambh─лrebhiс╕е pathibhiс╕е p┼лrviс╣Зebhiс╕е; and as second
half-verse it has our 3. 14 c, d. HGS. has ─Б y─Бta pitaraс╕е somy─Б
gambh─лraс╕е (misprint for -r─Бiс╕е?) pathibhiс╕е p┼лrvy─Бiс╕е, with an
altogether different c, d. We should prefer somy─Бsas unaccented,
both in this verse and in the next, but no ms. so reads. The comm. has
in c dadhata, which he pronounces the same as dhatta. In K─Бu┼Ы.,
in the pitс╣Ыnidhana ceremony, the verse accompanies (83. 27) the
bringing of the bone-relics, before sunset тМКinto the hut: Ke┼Ы.тМЛ; and it
is followed (83. 28, 29) by 1. 52 and 2. 29; then, in the
piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a (87. 28), the three are repeated; the comm. notices
only the latter use, stating that with this verse one is to scatter
sesame on the barhis spread for the purpose of giving the piс╣Зс╕Нas. In
number of syllables, the verse answers to the description of the Anukr.
(9+ 10: 11 + 11 = 41). тМКThe MB. reading makes a rectification of the
meter at the beginning of b.тМЛ

Griffith

Come hither, Fathers, who deserve the Soma, by the deep path- ways which the Fathers travel. Bestow upon us life and store of children, and favour us with increase of our riches.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Go away, O Fathers, delectable, by profound roads that go to the
    stronghold (p┼лry─Б╠Бс╣Зa); then, in a month, come ye again to our houses to
    eat the oblation, with good progeny, with good heroes.
Notes

All the pada-mss. commit the strange blunder of dividing ─Б╠Бy─Бta in
c into ─Б╠Б: ay─Бta; both editions make the necessary correction; the

Griffith

Depart, O Fathers, ye who merit Soma, by the deep pathways which the Fathers travel; But in a month, rich in fair sons and heroes, come back into our homes to eat oblation.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What one limb of you Agni J─Бtavedas left when making you go to the
    Fathers’ world, that same for you I fill up again; revel ye, O Fathers,
    in heaven (svarg├б) with [all] your limbs.
Notes

HGS. has (in ii. 11. 1) an analogous but quite different verse: yad vaс╕е
kravy─Бd an╠Дgam adahal lok─Бn ayam praс╣Зaya├▒ j─Бtaved─Бс╕е: tad vo тАЩham punar ─Б
ve┼Ыay─Бmy ariс╣гс╣н─Бс╕е sarv─Бir an╠Дg─Бiс╕е sam bhavata pitaraс╕е. Most of our mss.
(all except O.Op.R.), but, by his account, only one of SPP’s, leave
ajah─Бt in a unaccented; on the other hand, all without exception
accent in d pit├бras, which SPP. accordingly admits into his text;
but our emendation to pit├бras is plainly necessary. What the comm.
says is here unknown, because the manuscript shows a considerable
lacuna, involving the latter half of the explanation of this verse, with
the text of the next and the larger part of its exposition. K─Бu┼Ы. uses
the verse (88. 5) in the piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a, next after vss. 74, 78, to
accompany an offering of rice-grains with the stirring-stick (s─Бyavana
тМКthat is, sa-─Бyavana: SPP’s saс╣Бyavana, p. 233тБ┤, does not seem
rightтМЛ). тМКAs to completeness of limbs in the other world, see my note to
4. 12, above. This verse was translated metrically by Whitney, O. and
L.S., i. 57.тМЛ

Griffith

If Agni Jatavedas, as he bore you hence to the Fathers’ world, hath left one single. Limb of your bodies, here do I restore it. Fathers, rejoice in heaven with all your members!

Translation
  1. J─Бtavedas has been the messenger sent forth, at evening, at close of
    day to be honored by men;тАФthou hast given to the Fathers; they have
    eaten after their wont; eat thou, O god, the presented oblations.
Notes

We had the second half-verse above as 3. 42 c, d. Part of our mss.
(O.Op.R.D.), with, so far as appears, the majority of SPP’s, read in
b upav├бndyas, and the latter accordingly adopts it in his text;
the root vand does not appear to be anywhere else combined with upa.
The line reads like a kind of echo of RV. iv. 54. i тМКTB. iii. 7. 13тБ┤тМЛ.
The verse is the last one quoted in the piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a by K─Бu┼Ы. (89.
14), to accompany the withdrawal of the “extended” fires. тМКBy “extended”
I suppose W. means the technical praс╣З─лta (cf. comm., p. 233тБ╢). The
words of K─Бu┼Ы. are agnim praty─Бnayati: the ceremony seems to be the
same as that prescribed by ┼ЫB. at ii. 4. 2┬▓тБ┤, punar ulmukam api
sс╣Ыjati, and by ┼Ы┼ЫS. at iv. 5. 9, ulmukam agn─Бu kс╣Ыtv─Б.тМЛ

Griffith

Meet for men’s praises, Agni Jatavedas was sent as envoy when the day was closing. Thou gavest to the Fathers with oblation. They ate; eat, God, our offered sacrifices.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thou yonder, ho! hither thy mind! as sisters (j─Бm├н) a k├бkutsala,
    do thou cover him, O earth.
Notes

The translation implies the evidently necessary emendation to ├бs─Бu in
a; both editions give as─Б├║, because this is read by all the mss.;
the comm. understands the word as a vocative; it also reads the
interjection as h─Б, while the pada-text gives h─Б├н. It further
glosses j─Бmayas тМКalternativelyтМЛ with bhaginyas, and reads
kakutsthalam, explaining it as pradh─Бn─Бvayavaprade┼Ыam, and
paraphrasing with putr─Бd─лn─Бс╣Б ┼Ыiraс╕еprabhс╣Ыt─лny an╠Дg─Бni
┼Ы─лt─Бtapav─Бtaniv─Бraс╣З─Бya. The Pet. Lexx. conjecture kakutsala to be a
pet word for a little child. We had the third p─Бda above as 2. 50 d,
51 d, and 3. 50 d. K─Бu┼Ы. uses the verse (86. 10) with 2. 50 and
3. 49 in the ceremony over the bone-relics. The comm. includes with it
vs. 67.

Griffith

Here hast thou left thy heart; O man, as sisters leave their little pet. Do thou, O earth, envelop him.

  1. Loosen up the uppermost fetter from us, O Varuс╣Зa, [loosen] down

тМКwhich seeтМЛ; among our mss., only O.R. write it out in full. The comm.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Release from us all fetters, O Varuс╣Зa, with which one is bound
    crosswise, with which lengthwise; so may we live hundreds of autumns, by
    thee, O king, guarded, defended.
Notes

The rendering of sam─Бm├й and vy─Бm├й in b is far from certain: cf.
iv. 16. 8. The comm. explains: sam─Бmo n─Бma vy─Бmasaс╣Бj├▒itaprade┼Ы─Бt
saс╣Бkucitapram─Бс╣Зako de┼Ыaс╕е: saс╣Бnihite prade┼Ыe d┼лre prade┼Ыe ce тАЩti y─Бvat.
Two of our mss. (O.R.) and one of SPP’s read sam─Бn├й; and two or three
of the latter have badhyate, without accent. Nearly all, again, read
┼Ыar├бdam in c (our O.R.p.m. Land one of SPP’sтМЛ -das), and SPP.
admits ┼Ыar├бdam into his text; our -d─Бm is an emendation, and a
necessary one, unless we take instead -das, as in apposition with
┼Ыat─Б╠Бni. The comm. makes no difficulty of reading -dam, understanding
it, according to one of his convenient rules of interpretation, as a
sing. used in place of a plural. Most of our mss., again (except
P.O.Op.R.), but only one of SPP’s, accent r─Б╠Бjan. The comm. points out
that r├бkс╣гam─Бс╣З─Бs is for r├бkс╣гya-, which is altogether probable,
considering how easily a y is lost after с╣г or ┼Ы. The first p─Бda is
identical with vii. 83. 4 a. All the pada-mss. except one of SPP’s
read gupit─Б╠Б instead of -t─Б╠Бс╕е. The comm. directs the verse to be
recited for good fortune evening and morning at the end of the
da┼Ыar─Бtra in the pitс╣Ыmedha.

Griffith

From all those bonds, O Varuna, release us, wherewith a man is bound at length and cross-wise. Then may we live a hundred autumn seasons guarded by thee, O King, by thee protected.

Griffith

All Fathers who are here, the Fathers here are you: let then- follow you. May ye be the most excellent of these.

Translation
  1. They who are here, O FathersтАФalive here are weтАФ[be] they after
    us; may we be the best of them.
Notes

The translation here implies certain emendations of the text: pitaras
тМКaccentlessтМЛ in 87 and the first time in 86, and the omission of y├й
after the second pit├бras in 86: the latter is made also in our text,
while SPP. reads, with the mss., y├й тАШtra pit├бraс╕е pit├бro y├й тАШtra y┼лy├бс╣Б
sth├б. As to the accent of the pitaraс╕е pitaro in 86, the mss. are
wildly discordant, presenting every possible variation, and, considering
the many accentual blunders which they commit in this part of the text,
the details are not worth reporting, nor need we feel any hesitation in
amending to what seems to make the best sense. The omission of y├й is
much more serious, but seems demanded by the sense, and by the analogy
of 87. Similar passages are found in тМКTS. iii. 2. 5тБ╢,тМЛ TB. i. 3. 10тБ╕тБ╗тБ╣
тМКlike TS.тМЛ, and ┼Ы┼ЫS. iv. 5. 1 (the latter nearest like our text: ye
тАШtra pitaraс╕е pitaraс╕е stha y┼лyaс╣Б teс╣г─Бс╣Б ┼Ыreс╣гс╣нh─Б bh┼лy─Бstha: ya iha pitaro
manuс╣гy─Б vayaс╣Б teс╣г─Бс╣Б ┼Ыreс╣гс╣нh─Б bh┼лy─Бsma); compare also MS. i. 10. 3 and
A┼ЫS. ii. 7. 7.* All our mss. save one (Op.), and most of SPP’s, leave
stha in 86 unaccented; this non-accentuation, so far as it goes,
favors the omission of y├й. Bh┼лy─Бstha is a grammatically impossible
form, and should be emended to -sta, which is read by тМКTS. andтМЛ TB. in
the corresponding passage; ┼Ы┼ЫS., as has been seen, gives -stha. One of
SPP’s mss. has bh┼лy─Бsta. In 87, most of the mss. insert an avas─Бna
after smaс╕е, and SPP. follows them; it is of course senseless, unless
we use one also after stha in 86тАа; nor does the Anukr. appear to
acknowledge it, since it notes no difference of division as between the
two verses; but our тМКprintedтМЛ text at any rate blunders in not reading
either smo asm─Б╠Бn or smo тАШsm─Б╠Бn since it has omitted the
avas─Бna-mark. The metrical definitions of the Anukr. are worthless, as
there is no trace of meter in the two passages; they can by violence be
read into the number of syllables called for.

*тМКIn the second and third paragraphs below are given these passages
from TB., MS., and A┼ЫS. The TS. passage agrees with the TB. passage,
save that TS. has y├и тАШsm├нс╣Е lok├й for the very bad y├и тАШsmiс╣Е lok├й of
TB.тМЛ

тАатМКWe ought, I think, in fact to read with SPP. an avas─Бna-mark after
smaс╕е in vs. 87, not only as being abundantly supported by the mss. of
both editions, but also as called for by the sense and the general
(quadripartite) structure of the verse. And the same applies to the
reading of an avas─Бna-mark after stha in vs. 86; it is printed in
neither edition, but appears to be well warranted by the authorities of
both.тМЛ

тМКThe TB. passage, at i. 3. 10тБ╕тБ╗тБ╣, with the avas─Бnas as printed in the

lok├й ред m─Б╠Бс╣Б t├й тАШnu ред y├б et├бsmiс╣Е lok├й sth├б ред y┼лy├бс╣Б t├йс╣г─Бс╣Б v├бsiс╣гс╣нh─Б
bh┼лy─Бsta ред y├и тАШsmiс╣Е lok├й ред ah├бс╣Б t├йс╣г─Бс╣Б v├бsiс╣гс╣нho bh┼лy─Бsam.тАФThis
passage and its analogues have been discussed in two papers by
B├╢htlingk, Berichte der s├дchsischen Gesell., sessions of July 8, 1893,
and May 2, 1896. In the first, having the TB. passage before him, he
proposed to read, in place of the first sth├б, the word sy├║s, and to

smaс╕е (cf. Index, p. 41 b). Moreover, he suspects that the second

that p├бret─Бs offers a better antithesis to the j─лv─Б╠Бs of 87 (┼Ы┼ЫS.
manuс╣гy─Бs) than does the word pitaras itself; and the latter are

50, 54 above, also x. 6. 32.тАФApropos of the blunder bh┼лy─Бstha: reading
D─лgha Nik─Бya on the day of writing the above note, I observed at ix. 7,

with plural verb-ending, albeit the ek─Б makes the breach of common
concord most manifest and some mss. indeed read uppajjati. For the
like error, see xv. 7. 3: cf. also notes xiv. 2. 59; xviii. 3. 47.тМЛ

тМКThe MS. passage, p. 143тБ╢, is: eс╣г─Б╠Б yuс╣гm─Б╠Бkam pitaraс╕е: im─Б╠Б asm─Б╠Бkam: j─лv─Б╠Б

yuс╣гm─Бkam pitaraс╕е: im─Б asm─Бkam: j─лv─Б vo j─лvanta iha santaс╕е sy─Бma. To
this, G─Бrgya, in his vс╣Ыtti, adds: itik─Бr─Бdhy─Бh─Бreс╣Зa s┼лtracchedaс╕е:
santaс╕е sy─Бmeti mantraс╕е paс╣нhitavyo vaс╕еk─Бraс╣Б varjayitv─Б.тАФThe et─Бs and
im─Бs seem to refer to svadh─Б╠Бs (cf. ┼Ы┼ЫS. as above: y─Б atra pitarс╕еh

of MS. appears to require correction to et─Б╠Б p. et─Б╠Бс╕е.тМЛ

Griffith

All living fathers who are here are we here: let them follow us. May we be the most excellent of these.

реорео рдЖ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрдирдЗрдзреАрдорд╣рд┐ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Thee, O Agni, would we kindle, full of light (dyum├бnt), O god,
    unwasting; as that very wondrous fuel of thine shall shine in the sky
    (d├нv), bring thou food for thy praisers.
Notes

The verse is RV. v. 6. 4, and occurs also as SV. i. 419 and ii. 372, and
in TS. iv. 4. 4тБ╢ and MS. ii. 13. 7. All these agree together throughout,
reading in a te agna idh- for tv─Б тАЩgna idh-, and in c sy─Б╠Б
for s─Б╠Б. SPP. reads in c, with the comm., y├бd gha, and makes no
note upon it, implying that his mss. have the same; ours, however, give
y├бd dha (p. y├бt: ha), in accordance with the other texts. All the
mss. put an an avas─Бna between d and e тМКi.e. after dy├бviтМЛ,
and the Anukr. supports it, whence SPP. has it in his edition; we left
it out as being uncalled for, and wanting in the parallel texts. For the
use of the verse in K─Бu┼Ы. with 3. 42, see the note to the latter: cf. p.
871, ┬╢3.

Griffith

Bright Agni, we will kindle thee, rich in thy splendour, fading. not. So that this glorious fuel may send forth to heaven its light for thee. Bring food to those who sing thy praise.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The moon among the waters runs, an eagle in the sky (d├нv); they
    find not your track, O golden-rimmed lightnings: know me as such, O
    firmaments (r├│das─л).
Notes

The verse is RV. i. 105. 1 and also SV. i. 417 тМКTr─Бita S─БmanтМЛ; and its
first two p─Бdas are VS. xxxiii. 90 a, b; it is quoted by prat─лka
in GB. i. 2. 9; тМКp─Бda e is refrain all through the RV. hymn, save in
the last, the 19th, verseтМЛ. Both RV. and SV. read in d vidyutas,
as vocative, and the AV. mss. are divided between that and vidy├║tas;
SPP. has the former, which is to be preferred. The comm. repeats the
story of Trita and his two brothers, as “told by the ┼Ы─Бс╣нy─Бyanins,” in
almost precisely the same words as those in which it is given in the
commentator’s introduction to RV. i. 105. тМКOertel gives a summary
thereof, and also the corresponding passage, JB. i. 184, text and
version, JAOS. xviii.┬╣ p. 18-20.тМЛ тМКThe comm. quotes the verse as applied
in mah─Б┼Ы─Бnti called v─Бruс╣З─л in the Nakс╣гatra Kalpa, 18.тМЛ Why the verse
should be found as conclusion of this book of funeral hymns is very
obscure. тМКтШЮ See p. 1016.тМЛ

тМКHere ends the fourth anuv─Бka, with 1 hymn and 89 verses. The quoted

тМКHere also ends the thirty-fourth prap─Бс╣нhaka.тМЛ

Griffith

Within the waters runs the Moon, the strong-winged Eagle soars. in heaven. Ye Lightnings with your golden wheels, men find not your abid- ing-place. Hear this my call, O Heaven and Earth.

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рдкрд╛рджрдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: реорептИТ(рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╛рдГ) рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рд▓реЛрдХрдГ (рдЕрдкреНрд╕реБ) рд╕реНрд╡рдордгреНрдбрд▓рд╕реНрдереЗрд╖реБ рдЬрд▓реЗрд╖реБ (рдЕрдиреНрддрдГ) рдордзреНрдпреЗ (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рд╕реБрдкрд░реНрдгрдГ) рдзрд╛рдкреДрд╡рд╕реНрдпрдЬреНрдпрддрд┐рднреНрдпреЛ рдирдГред рдЙреж рейредремред рд╕реБ+рдкреДрдкрд╛рд▓рдирдкреВрд░рдгрдпреЛрдГ-рди рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГред рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рдкреВрд░рдпрд┐рддрд╛ (рдзрд╛рд╡рддреЗ) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ (рджрд┐рд╡рд┐) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдпрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ (рди) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рд╣рд┐рд░рдгреНрдпрдиреЗрдордпрдГ) рд╣рд░реНрдпрддреЗрдГ рдХрдиреНрдпрдиреН рд╣рд┐рд░реНрдЪред рдЙрежрелредрекрекред рд╣рд░реНрдп рдЧрддрд┐рдХрд╛рдиреНрддреНрдпреЛрдГ-рдХрдиреНрдпрдиреНред рдирд┐рдпреЛ рдорд┐рдГред рдЙреж рекредрекрейред рдгреАрдЮреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдгреЗ-рдорд┐ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГредрд╣рд┐рд░рдгреНрдпреЗ рдХрдордиреАрдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкреЗ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдордирд┐ рдиреЗрдорд┐рдГ рд╕реАрдорд╛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рддреЗ рддрдерд╛рднреВрддрд╛рд╕реНрддрддреНрд╕рдореНрдмреБрджреНрдзреМ (рдкрджрдореН) рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд┐рдореН (рд╡рд┐рдиреНрджрдиреНрддрд┐) рд▓рднрдиреНрддреЗ (рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддрдГ) рд╡рд┐+рджреНрдпреБрддрджреАрдкреНрддреМ-рдХреНрд╡рд┐рдкреНред рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рдирд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдГ (рд╡рд┐рддреНрддрдореН) рдЬрд╛рдиреАрддрдореНред рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рдХреБрд░реБрддрдореН (рдореЗ)рдордо (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) рд╡рдЪрдирд╕реНрдп (рд░реЛрджрд╕реА) рд╣реЗ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд┐рд╡ рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖реМ рее
